**`/Users/bruno/siopv/.ignorar/agent-persona-research-2026-03-09/002_llm-agent-behavioral-control-guardrails-techniques.md`**

## Summary of findings

The report covers 10 sections across ~2,500 words with 30+ sources. Key highlights:

**Highest-impact techniques discovered:**

1. **Prompt Repetition** (Google Research, Dec 2025) -- simply repeating the prompt yields up to 76% accuracy improvement on non-reasoning tasks, with zero latency cost. Theoretically grounded in causal masking limitations.

2. **Context Rot is controllable** (arXiv, Oct 2025) -- drift follows stable equilibria, not runaway decay. Simple reminder interventions reliably reduce divergence.

3. **Agent Stability Index (ASI)** (arXiv, Jan 2026) -- first formal metric for agent drift, measuring 12 dimensions across semantic, coordination, and behavioral drift.

4. **Manus AI's production patterns** -- todo.md for attention anchoring, file-system-as-memory, context-aware state machine with logit masking for tool control, KV-cache optimization (10x cost difference between cached/uncached tokens).

5. **Persona prompting is overrated for accuracy** -- empirically proven to control style/tone but NOT factual accuracy. CrewAI's role-goal-backstory pattern works because it combines persona with task constraints, not because of the persona alone.

6. **Three-layer guardrails** (input/interaction/output) are now industry standard, with OpenAI's tripwire mechanism as the cleanest halt-on-violation pattern.

7. **Compaction-safe instructions** require structural redundancy: critical rules in system prompt + external files + periodic re-injection. The `<!-- COMPACT-SAFE -->` marker pattern (already used in SIOPV) aligns with best practices.

Section 10 provides SIOPV-specific recommendations for the hexagonal architecture, LangGraph orchestration, verification pipeline, and multi-phase handoffs.</result>

## [2026-03-09T05:21:23.588Z] Queue Operation: enqueue

<task-notification>
<task-id>a9181c2cc6b3b351d</task-id>
<tool-use-id>toolu_01XToSp3QJcwKGw5ymBa9bvh</tool-use-id>
<status>completed</status>
<summary>Agent "Research Claude Code agent personas" completed</summary>
<result>Report saved to `/Users/bruno/siopv/.ignorar/agent-persona-research-2026-03-09/001_claude-code-agent-persona-guardrails-behavioral-control.md`.

**Summary of key findings:**

1. **Agent definition files** use YAML frontmatter (16 supported fields) + Markdown body as system prompt. Only `name` and `description` are required. The body IS the persona -- subagents receive only this prompt, not the full Claude Code system prompt.

2. **The 150-instruction ceiling** is real and researched: compliance degrades uniformly as instruction count increases. Keep the 20 most critical rules; handle the rest with hooks or tool restrictions.

3. **Three-tier guardrails**: Prompts are requests (~80% compliance), tool restrictions are deterministic (100%), hooks are deterministic (100%). The single most important insight: "Rules in prompts are requests. Hooks in code are laws."

4. **PreToolUse is the only blocking hook** among 16 hook events. It can deny operations via exit code 2 or JSON `permissionDecision: "deny"`. Starting in v2.0.10, it can also modify tool inputs before execution.

5. **Anti-improvisation** works best through: per-step constraint design (different constraint types per step), tool restriction allowlists, maxTurns limits, todo list recitation (pushes plan to end of context for recency attention), and fresh context windows.

6. **Context positioning**: LLMs attend most to start and end of context. Front-load critical rules in agent body, repeat the most important rule at both start and end, use emphasis markers (IMPORTANT, YOU MUST), and keep total loaded instructions under 150.

7. **Production patterns**: Trail of Bits runs bypass-permissions with OS sandboxing; SuperClaude defines 16 cognitive personas as .md context configurations; Adaline Labs uses a guardrails ladder (read-only -> scoped changes -> PR-ready with checks).

The report includes specific SIOPV recommendations in Section 9 covering agent body templates, hook configurations, and a layered guardrails strategy for each verification agent.</result>

</task-notification>

6. **Agent Persona Templates** -- 4 complete templates (Scanner ~50 lines, Researcher ~60 lines, Summarizer ~65 lines, Orchestrator ~80 lines), all under the 200-line limit, following the 4-element pattern (identity + expertise + constraints + output format), with front-loaded critical rules, end-repeated #1 rule, explicit "You are NOT" constraints, and 5-item DO NOT lists.
